Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes descend from the veins that are on top of the head due to heat, and medical treatment does not help, and you see the face of the patient redden, and feel a trembling on the forehead as if shivering;
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and when the eyes are inflamed and moist so that the hairs of the eyelids fall out, and the eyelids are heated, and are peeled by the ardor of tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And the ancients called it "contusion cure," and it is that you remove the hairs from the forehead of the patient who has this disease, then make three cuts on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and one of the cuts should be about two inches right in the middle of the forehead going downwards to the nose, and the other two at the sides above the eyelids, and be careful not to cut the arteries that are on the two sides above the eyelids;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and keep your hand away from the joining of the two jawbones, and let each wound be the quantity of three fingers across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have prepared a piece of sponge and much cloth for wiping the blood, then apply the sharp spatula in two parts where this is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision which is above the temple to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and peel everything that is between the two cuts to the entire surface which is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then extract with this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	so put in the first cut the instrument which is called "cultellaire", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the sharp side towards the flesh affected by the disease, and the blunt side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous up to where it opens from the heart, and then make another one in the middle cut up to the other side;
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then draw blood evenly, and press the area for the blood taken;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then put in each cut a wick of old cotton, and place on top cloths moistened with wine and oil and assafetida, and be careful that no hot abscess comes near;
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day loosen the bandage, and apply a great deal of warm water, then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments used to heal wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the realm of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When a person frequently gets acute catarrh, and you see the eyes dull and small, and weakened vision, and the eyelids burned;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and on the head it causes a painful headache, and the patient sneezes;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then you know by these accidents that those materials and the catarrh do not come from anywhere else but from many veins, and the remedy that is best, is this one.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you instruct the patient to lie down with his head backwards, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another on the wider side.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin from the temple on the left to the temple on the right, and let the incision go as far as the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move during eating;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then separate the two edges of the cut and put old cotton and linen threads in between;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then bind above with cloths moistened in wine and in oil, and beware of a hot abscess;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is removed, then you must rub the bone until cartilage begins to grow, then treat it with drying substances, which promote the hardening of the cartilage.
En teil maniere:	In such manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	take two parts of wheat flower, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and administer it to these wounds to promote the hardening of cartilage throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the treatment for ear congestion
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that falls into the ears is one of the four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or grain, or animal, or stone of mine or similar things such as iron;
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seed, such as beans, peas, lentils;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or fluid things such as water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or any other kind of thing that does not fit in the ear and does not grow in the ear falls in, place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, then distill a little violet oil or flaxseed oil, then apply extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and make the person sneeze with condyse, and plug the nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place around the ear pieces of cloth or wool;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and pull the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Very often force comes from this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if force does not come, the administrator should perform extraction with fine tweezers, of which here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If force comes with the tweezers, it is good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, then perform the extraction with a fine needle of small double thread;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not come out by this means, then make a tube of lead and put the end of the tube into the opening of the ear firmly, and plug what is around the tube with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the tube;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then strongly draw the force, for often comes force as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come with force in such manner, then take glue from coagulated substance used by fowlers, and place some instrument that is sharp for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	then press the glue on the stone or whatever it may be, and draw force.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	and if it does not come out by force from all these things that we have said, then hasten to split the ear before a hot abscess and spasm comes.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the method of the splitting is that you first bloodlet the patient from the cephalic vein, and draw blood according to the measure of his strength, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear in the fat where it hangs.
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the cut be like a moon, until you come to the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it hastily with your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, then administer extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot come out, then administer the spatulum gently according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and to administer an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think the grains are moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract with fine tweezers and the sucker, as we have said, so that the extraction is light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of water that enters the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use sneezing with preliminary condiments, and plug the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out through that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If not, then take many stones according to the length of your thumb, thin and light, and warm them a bit in the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and place them in the patient's ear orifice, and strike with one of his feet from the other side, and hit with another stone on the stone that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not stop striking stone with stone until all the pus comes out completely, and thus it will come out entirely;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you wish, take some reed, and put one end in the ear, and the other end press against fire until the softer part of the reed is burned;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then make another part of other incisions until all the pus comes out, just as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of the creature, if it is of small body, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the section;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is of large body that can be felt, then apply the extraction with tweezers;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and it is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of earwigs from the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the section and in the treatment of distillations, and the treatment does not help, then you must look into the ear in the sunlight:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If there are any hairs visible, pull them out with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, then take the tube of which this is the shape:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And put the finest end into the ear according to the extent of the patient's suffering, then suck forcefully on the entire tube;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, stuff around the tube with cotton as I have said in the stone;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not come out as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have tested in the excision of worms, and you will find them in the treatise on distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and so distill your oils and your medicines into the ear with all this instrument, of which here is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	and whether it is made of silver or bronze, it should be wide below the small openings, and above narrower for distilling;
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press inside the distillation, there is an instrument of bronze well made for this purpose, and if you want, take the scraper and wrap around the tip appropriately with cotton;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then pour your oil or your juice, and what you want of your medicines into the tube, and the tube should be in the ear;
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then push the scraper into all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled into the eardrum;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the patient feels it inside, and let the distillations be slightly heated over fire before they are distilled into the ear;
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and beware that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the treatment for ear congestion
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	Some children are born who have no openings in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and the same thing happens to adults due to blockage from a wound, or flesh grown inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes occur deeply within the ear so that one cannot see them;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and sometimes the opening is slightly obscured, and one can see it clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	Then that which comes in secret, so that it cannot be seen, is of severe healing in many conditions, and in that which can be seen you must place the patient's ear to the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the obstruction evident, then the work has all this space where the form is:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And let it be sharp and cutting on both front and back entirely smooth, so that it does not injure the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the obstruction is of flesh or body of the ear, then hold it with fine tweezers, and cut lightly, until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the obstruction is deeply in the ear, then take a fine and light scraper and warm it slightly over fire, then place it in the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the need to scrape where the patient feels pain in the ear, do it lightly, and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then put in the ear a plug according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this for some days until the wound is sealed, or you take a plug and moisten it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on it;
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear swollen, then you must remove the plug and insert another moistened with an ointment made of rose oil and wax until the swelling is gone;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge and cloths in cold water, and place them on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are in the chapter on hemorrhages.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of paperflies
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This eyelid that comes over the eyes when they are moist and dry, you should stretch it with tweezers and forceps, and cut it from its roots with a spatula;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then apply ground vitriol to the area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if it does not heal, then cauterize it with a fine lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision is very useful;
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and they often recur if anything remains of their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times come in the eye membranes things that resemble hail in their form and hardness, and for this reason is this disease called "hail", and it is a collection of moisture thickened above and below the membrane;
li ovraiges est telz:	the work is such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	be careful if the hail moves from one side to another, and it is an easy thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	then make an incision widely, then gently scrape each part, then take it with tweezers, and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	if you cannot cut it without piercing a bit of the membrane, then do not worry about the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the wound is large, then it is sewn with a stitch, and treat until it is healed;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, then do not use any force, for the ointments restore it quickly and enhance the flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the earwax is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then invert the paper, and stretch the earwax with tweezers, and cut and press from both sides;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is moved away by the incision, it does not matter;
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the earwax is cut, then lift the salt water oil, and treat the area with something that enhances flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a fat that is tangled in the web of the eyelids above, and this happens more to children than to other people, and greatly troubles their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and because of this they lie on their faces immediately, and sleep thus, and their eyelids under their eyebrows are moist which swells up and the appearance is covered by the exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the method of the work is that the patient puts his head in your hand;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach contained in each part, then place it on it;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your hands from one side to the other, so that the protrusion is gathered within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then cut in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a wide split, and let it not be larger than the wound one makes at the site of the vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and cut the skin thoroughly until you reach the protrusion;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in various positions, the protrusion comes out of the split, according to the form of a white fatty piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Then extract it with a piece of coarse cloth held between your hands to the wind, and turn your hand right and left until it is scattered;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and take care not to insert into the fissure, that you do not reach all the way to the spleen until the eye, that you do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	and if the abscess does not open at the beginning of the fissure, then slightly enlarge the fissure gently until it opens;
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths with oil and water, and place them on the area, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are such people who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the place hot, then treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	the hairs of the armpits
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When on the eyelids hairs grow in a manner other than natural and are irritated, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases such as habitual tearing and softening of the eyelids and leukoma, to the point that it can lead to the destruction of the eyes;
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and the treatment according to four methods:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by cautery with fire together, or by medicine applied according to what is mentioned before in the chapter of cautery, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by splints, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient on your lap, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	if it is turned, it is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, then put a needle with the whole thread on top;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let it be near the edge of the paper where the hair grows next to these hairs, and pull the thread across the entire paper, and turn it to the razor;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then cut into the part below the skin, below the attached hairs, all through the spatiumille cutting, from the large tear sheet to the small;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then extract the thread, and place below the skin a small tent of cotton and cloth, then sign on the skin a figure of enche, like the leaf of myrtle, and always it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you wish to lift the divided skin.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And there are cases where it is necessary to cut a large quantity of the skin according to how softened the skin is;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then cut through the entire spatiumille along the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the large tear sheet to the small;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs with the thickness of a root, then insert the lancet into one of the two angles of the boil, then peel it all;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then bring the two lips together with a stitch of one needle and all the thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and make the excess of threads on both eyebrows stick with some sticky things, if you wish to do this;
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if not, then do not bother, then leave the stitch and the threads for three or four days;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then treat the wound without stitching with drying and binding substances, for the bandage raises the wound at its closure and assembly, but the stitch is weak (as the ancients say), and this is work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere:	and there is another method:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you mark the paper with a figure which is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have described, at three inches apart according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what exceeds the small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	and if you are not able to hold the tweezers, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with a thread, and put it through the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and place one thread next to the large eyelid, and the second thread next to the small one, and gather the threads equally between your fingers;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin where you have marked, as we have described, then bring together the two edges of the wound by stitching, and care for it until it is healed;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with poultice and similar soothing ointments;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyelid turn inward:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	then you must use what we have said about the incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the suturing in one and the other is more intricate.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of hernias is according to this method:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and it is that you turn the eyelid inside and make an incision according to what I have said, and then make two hernias by art, and two subtle threads as long as the eyelid and the width of the spatula are;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut at the two shoulders of two parts where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then carefully join one and the other on top of what protrudes from the paper of the eye, and fully extract the two channels from the two parts;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and leave it this way for some days, and the skin that was constricted will die, dry out, and peel off, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it takes too long, cut it with force, then treat it until it is healed;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is sealed, and the paper is removed, the hairs will no longer prick;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and this is the form of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the work is such that you take a fine needle, and put in it a thread of silk smooth and fine;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then gather the shoulders and sew one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long;
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then arrange in the case another fine thread of silk briefly, and sew the ends of the thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	then have the patient place his head in your hand;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and place it near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for this is subtle and minute work, then insert the needle all the way into the case at the root of the hair adjacent, and pierce quickly through the parchment until you pull it over the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then pull out the hair up to the socket, and place that hair in the socket, if there is one or two or three or more;
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then withdraw your hand until the hair comes out of the socket entirely into the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the socket is pulled and the hair does not come out with it, then pull the socket downward along the thread that you have arranged there, until the socket comes out of the upper hole and you can see it with your eye;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	then pull the socket and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair burns in its place and new flesh grows over;
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	and if the hair is short, then accompany the long hair with natural curly hair, and lift it with that which you leave, until it is extended and then raise it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the pus from the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the corruption comes to the eye, it happens in two ways:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by the suddenness of a wound, or of cutting or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the method of treatment is that you split that suturing, and separate its lips, and put linen threads inside, and keep it tied until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not appropriate that you use in its treatment things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, then the illness returns worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but use things that soften, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the juice of water or alcohol and flaxseed should be cooked, and anointment of aquilon melted in any of the oils, and it is wrapped in a cloth, and it is cured with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your care is that you take heed that it does not heal in the same form as before;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these works that we have mentioned are only precautions for this illness, so that it does not return in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness that is beneath is truly called "axacrati," and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from wound and cut and cautery and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the method of the work in it is that you take a needle, in which there is double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left eyelid to the right, so that the thread comes out two fingers away from the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then stretch the flesh above all the needle, and cut it with a spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is necessary, it is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	if not, then take a scraper and put it in the cut, and turn the paper, and make two cuts on the side within the paper;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and let the heads of the two fissures from the two corners of the incision you have made be such that when they are joined together, the figure is like that of a letter called "Greek I";
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then remove that flesh according to the amount its sides are sharp beneath, from what lies under the skin, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with what we have said about mollifying medicines and poultices until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the disease comes from a fissure or suture or cautery, then you must make a complete incision beneath the hairs of the skin, according to what is stated above;
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then separate between the two sides of a tent, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters devise by all their power how they might restore the figure to its natural shape;
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patient himself, according to what is required of work and instruments in various arrangements.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the suddenness of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this soldering happens to men in such a way that the eyelid above is welded with the white of the eye, and cannot move nor perform its natural functions, then you must put the point of a razor under the eyelid, and lift it up;
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and you stretch the eyelids, until you cut that which is hard with a fine spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient cannot bear it if the spatula too sharp does not wound the eye;
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and let your incision, with which you peel that assembly, be slight, so that the paper returns to its natural form;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and the entire assembly is healed, and they sometimes use salty water in the eye, and wash it with fresh water, and with collyria;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then place between the paper and the eye a linen tent, and put on the eye wool soaked in egg white;
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after the third day use the collar and of sudatory things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the nail grows in two ways:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	it is nervous and similar to hard skin, and another that is not nervous, but resembles white frozen moisture, which when touched with iron and thought to be treated with tweezers, one cannot.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and both appearances begin near the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover the entire sight and all the light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the method of the incision is that the patient place his head in your hand, then you operate on the eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lift the paper to your hand, then bend the nail with small tweezers, and stretch it out above;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and put horse hair, or cow hair, or ox hair, and strong thread;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the tip of the needle a bit and insert it into the nail, and pierce through the entire nail, and tie the nail with thread and stretch it out above, and scrape all the hair along the side of the nail that faces the eyeball and sew the hair to the top, then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear duct thoroughly and with small force, and leave the natural flesh in the tear duct so that tears do not come from the usual path due to the incision;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and sometimes the nail extends only to the ounce, and to the thread, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then one peels off all the spathumille from which this form is made:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	and be careful that the spathumille does not touch the flesh membrane and break it, and that the pupil is not perforated;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision, put a bit of ground collyrium in the eye, and of the collar made of litharge, and leave it until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cleanse it with what is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	and if the nail is not firm, and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this nail-like condition is often treated with medicines;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and they grow as I have described in the division, and if you wish to cut them, then work the eye of the patient, and take the spatula light point sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And scrape the nail above carefully, and if you see that it does not become finer and the rasp is pressed in, then drip from your mouth into the eye a mixture made of litharge and red collyrium and well ground, and plug the eye until the next day;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then begin the other work according to this same method, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If anything is not contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then leave it alone and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh of the lacrimal apparatus harms the eye greatly, then suspend it with an awl, and cut part of it but not all, so that tears do not come from it;
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	then distill into the eye red collyrium which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	In the eyes of some men sometimes red flesh grows, and covers the pupil and rises up on the eyelids and turns them outward, and looks like a pomegranate flower;
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the procedure is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then you work on the eyes, and cut all that flesh with appropriate forceps for this, and hold it firmly;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then cut the first layer of flesh, and keep cutting down to the scraper until the end, and be careful not to injure the eye during the procedure;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and let the incision of the spatumile, which we have described in the incision of the nail and the small forceps with which the sebel is removed, be as the form after this chapter demonstrates;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, then apply oil of selvedge ground in which you add red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines, and place on it oil-soaked cotton with egg white, so that it is secured from a hot abscess;
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if anything remains and the skin swells, and you fear a hot abscess, then leave the oil and treat the abscess with things that soothe a hot abscess;
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do when flesh is attached by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	but nevertheless, you must lighten the treatment of each weak eye along the natural course;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and of the accidental vein, in ironwork;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this limb is able to endure the work.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Films are red veins that cover the eye, and they hinder the sight's work and weaken the eye all day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is then necessary first that you look if the eye in which the cataract is, is protruding, and there is no other disease except the cataract;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then treat it in this manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to place his head in your hand, then suspend those veins for all the ancon according to your wisdom, and let the ancons be finely doubled according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two incisions by degrees on the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then when you bind those veins subtly with force, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see those veins move out of the eye;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and be careful not to injure the eye with the tips of the spatulas, and do this work at midday in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not cut outside those veins;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, distilled green and red collyrium in the eye to corrupt what remains of the bile.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you are not able to extract all of this in that hour, then apply a plaster on the eye made of things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is soothed and you are sure there is no risk of a hot abscess, then restart according to this method described above until he is healed;
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The doctor calls a fistula "arissati":
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then it is necessary that you cut into the abscess where it should be opened, and draw out all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then remove it all with this instrument of which here is the form;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "aspre chief," and it should be made of iron to the length of the head, and pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And put on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a bit until you know that that corruption is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the wound is sealed, and flesh grows, and the core of the boil is sealed, and remains thus for forty days, and it does not renew or become an abscess, and no adverse incidents occur, know that it is healed;
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	if not, then there is another method to bring the fistula to the opening of the nose in this manner:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and it is that you uncover the bone for the second time by iron, and with aqueous medicines, and when it is uncovered then take the burin in this manner, and let the head of the iron be three-angled, and the handle be tapered to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then place it on the bone near the eyelid, and remove your hand from the eye by a little, then turn the entire drill until it penetrates the bone and the patient feels it because wind comes out if he holds his hand over his nose;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the eye with dry medications, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and the eyelids harden, the matter goes to the nose;
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eye is fully opened and nothing obstructs the nose, nor any reduction, then you must bind the patient;
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then heal it, then apply cupping or a hot poultice without bleeding to suction, then place on the eye a dressing made of acacia, aloe, frankincense, and sarcocolle, and then close the eye, and cover it with bandages and cloths;
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the method of the cloths is that you take cloths sufficiently soft, and fold each in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the amount that the eye may need;
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then strain it over a hard bandage firmly, and begin the suction cups to suck without pricking;
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the swelling softens, you must strain it very tightly;
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then remove the bandage after the day and night, and if you see the eye improving, it is good;
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	so begin again the plaster and the cloths and the binding and the cupping until he is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the rupture of green thread
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When disruptions come to the uvea, it opens up, and small pieces like grains of resin appear, which are astonishing to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	then if you see to cut it, the procedure is such that you insert a needle at the root from the lower part up to the upper part, then insert another needle where there is double thread from the tear area;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and have it pierced, and leave the first needle according to the position;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then cut the area of the double thread and tie a part of the uvea around it tightly, then remove the needle and put on the eye moistened wool in egg white;
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it until the flesh falls with the grape, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and sometimes the wound is restrained by the grape all around with a circle of cloth until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eye shows great opacity, pierce it with a fine needle that comes through the pupil, and draw out the white moisture and lower the eye, and let it enter at once;
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the white of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing more than phlegm gathered in the eye, resembling descending water, but it is not water;
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make sit the patient on the prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the vein come up to your eyes;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then let it be fixed, and do not lower and let the light be dispersed, and the patient sees things as he was accustomed;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend below, know that it is acute, and if the descending of the vein is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	then make the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine spatula and cut on the corneal membrane a spot by the continuity of the conjunctiva with the corneal membrane and the corona until the vein appears;
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is issued, then let distilled into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek has been boiled and honey, then be cleaned by another cleaning until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have seen the likenesses of waters in the division, and what is needed for piercing;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	then work according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the sunlight, cover the healthy eye and press very hard;
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then place the eye paper on your left hand if the eye is left, or on your right hand if the eye is right;
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right;
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	then place the tip of the instrument near the crown by the thickness of a nail in that swelling of the eye at the part with fewer tears, then insert the instrument which is called "almagda" forcefully, and turn your hand until it pierces into the swelling of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty space;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is necessary that the length of the path of almagda be exactly according to the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the black part;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and it is the crown of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	and you will see the bone on that paper because of the clarity of the corneal membrane, then place the instrument just where the fluid is, then press under one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the aqueous humor is now dislodged, the patient sees in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After rest a little, and if the fluid rises through the second pathway, apply force with the instrument, and when it is fixed in and does not rise, then extract the substance gently by rotating your hand little by little;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put in a bit of clear gem water, and bathe the eye with it.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply to the eye wads or wool soaked in rose oil and egg white, and bind with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply ground cumin with egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, for there are such men who have too hard eyes, then you must take the instrument which is called "alberit", of which here is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make the place delicate, then insert the substance as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and at the completion of the work prepare the patient so that the doctor is suitable, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place;
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and be deprived of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and be bound according to his condition until the third day;
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then untie him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then bind him again until the seventh day;
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not right that you do this at the hour of the treatment or after the incision now, but you must lighten this, because the fluid rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	When abscesses become hot, that you unbind the eye before the seventh day, and apply what alleviates abscesses;
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is calmed, then unbind the sight and place on his face a bandage to cover for some days, and let him remain in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then let him leave the house little by little, and he should return to his normal activities;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and know that no student should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from Yemen, who told us that in his country they make a device pierced, to which one sucks the water, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and by chance it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, for those who do not understand them see them;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and let them be properly made of bronze:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of these be of the same fineness, and the back in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Sometimes diverse charmed objects are born or arise, some of which resemble scorpions with many legs;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and there are some in which a fox-colored charm is embedded, and it has a good-colored sow.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that case, with the charm that is in the form of a sow and not embedded, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and works its nostrils, and throws the incense at those cars, and pulls them away;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	then cut what you can support with the subtle sharp spatula on one side, until you know that the car is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if anything remains that cannot be cut, then open it with all the subtle light instruments, so that nothing remains;
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if it swells up, or the abscess is hot, then treat it accordingly;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if these are malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize it until the swelling is subsided and all the cars are removed, then apply salted water or vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the nose bleeds, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that he is healed;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if moisture does not come out as it should, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, which the instruments do not reach to cut:
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	then it is necessary that you put in a slightly thick linen thread, and it should be tied by skilled hands, and have between each knot a space of one inch or less;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and have the patient place the end of the thread in his nose with some force, and pull it through until it comes from inside the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and often children do this in schools, and it is an easy thing for one who wants to do it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	Then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and pull one after the other along the threads that are in the string.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the gnats have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the string, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of the flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put a plug of linen in the nose for several days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them;
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument for cleansing the head, to which one drips oils and medicines at its base:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	and whether it is of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and the conduit likewise;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instruments be full to cleanse the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and let it have a handle at the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Often, a disease called "telul" arises on the head from the base, and it grows and becomes large quickly, so that it is a noticeable thing to look at;
