Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the throwing of stones, and the cutting of sword and knife, or spear or staff or arrow, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or they are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for the remedy will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, then take care if it is from the throwing of stones or similar things, and the skin is entirely ruptured and the wound is large, and you fear the rising of a hot abscess:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	so that he may bleed from the cephalic vein especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be opposite to the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and prevent the patient from excess of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not wish to bleed, then his food should be reduced, and he should drink no wine, nor eat any meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and apply to the wound, if hot abscesses come, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in astringent wine;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the fresh wound, which has all its blood and is not exposed to the air, powder, which I will mention a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the burn has moved, then apply some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword cut and similar ones, and the edges cannot be brought together by bandages, then bring them together by stitching, just as I will say about abdominal wounds, of the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	if the wound is exposed to the bone, and can, and holds only to a bit, then cut it;
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat hearty foods, such as heads and cooked wheat, as well as beans, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	and if you find rotten flesh on the skin, and it is not near the bone, then cut all the rot out and discard it, then treat the wound;
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery or vein in the wound that cannot be stopped by medicine, then seek the artery, and if you find it separated, tie it with a thread;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help at all, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and it is that you put this powder which soothes as soon as the fire has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the method of the powder is as follows:
pren encens une partie;	take frankincense one part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	live charcoal three parts, and powder it finely, and apply to the wound, and press it firmly until it dries well and adheres to all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then strain it well, and leave it unloosened if it does not swell;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes this is done with coals alone, when one does not have the incense or the dragon's blood, but the fire has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the burn has moistened the wound, especially in this state, one does not apply this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digestion ointments, or powder of barley flour made with water and honey, until it gives off pus;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you hereafter the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	if it is the nerve, there is no other method but to leave the treatment alone, and not apply anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their connection to it is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be warm, such as hot water mixed with sweet water, and blended with rose oil, and cucumber also washed in sweet water, and other minerals according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is covered and full of pus, pierce it at the lowest point;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and bleeding comes out, then open it, tie it up, and cauterize it if necessary;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the conduit is preserved so that the flesh can pass, then sew the windpipe to the neck bone, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural form;
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind it appropriately, and leave it for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then remove it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are bone fragments, then pull out all that you can, and for those you cannot remove, leave them until the wound becomes rotten, and is separated and the discharge is lightened;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I have said in his chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a stab from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, then check if wind comes out of the wound when the patient breathes:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	then you know that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put the powder at the first hour, nor bind it because the blood does not clot perfectly, and returns to the heart, and kills the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you do not have an ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to draw out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	then there will not come spasm, nor trembling from the heart, nor strangeness of alien influence;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good signs, then know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with bandages and other treatments until it is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal and continues to discharge, then know that there is a fistula;
si la cure si com on doit.	treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	and if the wound is from the incision of a sword or knife, and it is simple, whether on the buttocks or the back, treat the part that is in front;
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, by suturing;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, by powder; and if it is compressed in the bone, and has been chopped into pieces, gather the wound, and pull out the fragments if they are separated;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not removed, let the wound fester, it will lighten the extraction;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is the same as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the belly is great and moderate and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the large wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines come out, causing intrusion of other substances;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because one delays in putting the intestines back in place, if they are not put back continuously;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	For the reason that the intestines swell immediately when they feel the cold, they retract more deeply, and for this the middle wound is beneficial, for it allows the intestines to be moved back into place more than the other two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the two common sutures happen in the belly suture, and the suture of other body wounds and the two other specific sutures are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and nevertheless they are more specific with the belly suture, and I will say one by one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine comes out, and it is difficult to put back, this is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	For the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is crushed, warm it in such a manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	soak a sponge or a piece of cloth in warm water only, or you boil in water squill and cinnamon and spike, and moisten the intestines until the swelling is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes this is done with wines that constrict, and it is better to use only one for reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling begin to subside, moisten the intestines with water in which nettles and mallows have been boiled, for by this the entrance is made easier for small things;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then cut slightly into the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is to reduce the swelling, which none should cut unless there is great necessity;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for making the incision:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	then cut inside the curvature and not further, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, put them back in place according to their natural form in their proper place, if you can, for this is worth doing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part below the belly, then you must make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the part below the belly, then raise the head and chest higher than the parts below, and likewise if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, then place your attention so that the wounded part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus one must administer what I say in large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	In small wounds apply what is prepared for you, then have between your hands the pitious minister who thoroughly closes all the rupture with his hand, and brings together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common method of sutures, which is that you take one needle or more, according to the width of the wound, then leave at the head of the wound some space, and insert a needle with strong thread;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two sides of the skin with the two sides of the sinew, which is beneath the skin inside, until you pierce that part, and bring together the two ends of the sinew all four together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then strain a double thread around the needle in two parts, then bring together the two edges of the wound properly, and then leave one finger's width, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then twist the thread like you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to how many needles you need, until the entire wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be of medium size, between fine and thick, for the fine needles cut all the flesh, and those too thick cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for that reason, they should be of medium size;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it is not right to push the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, so that they do not cut and work the wound before the suturing;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cut the heads of the needles so they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and put cloths or towels on the heads of the needles to keep them still, and leave them until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, for it requires one or two needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitching is common, and it is when you bring together the two sides of the skin and the two sides of the flesh together with one needle using one strong medium thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced these four sides together, then return the needle to the part where you began, in the manner one sews clothes;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and place between each stitch the thickness of a small finger;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	this stitch served the man, and I sewed a wound that a man had in his belly, which was cut by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and the intestines came out about two palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been outside for 24 hours, and the wound was sutured until 15 days, and I treated it, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat it with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and push it from the outer part to the inner part;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the center straight through, then place the head of the thread where you have pushed the needle, and make it pierce from the inner part to the outer part;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the meaning of this stitch is that you sew as skinners do with skins, and that you leave one side once, and take it from the other side, until the stitches are completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of stitching, which Galien properly described, is such that some use to join the two parts naturally together, and bring one end of the thread to the other end in such a manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	stick a needle at the head of the mirach that is close, and make pierce that place only, and leave the two cheeks of the syfac;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part to the inner part, at the two cheeks of the syfac;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make pierce one and the other from the outer part to the inner part, at two other cheeks of the mirach that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most difficult manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galien said this word, and some testify that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having thread;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle from one side, and another from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is more severe than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, although the iron has moved it, you must reset the intestine, and the stitch;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put the healing powder on it, and if the iron has moved it, then put some ointment that is available on it, until the wound draws;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and they cut the threads, and the scissors are soldered, and the mirrors;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound like the others until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you do not have medicines, then put on it, as soon as it starts to expel pus, old cotton, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need other medicines in many cases when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you fear that the wound may spread to the principal limbs, then you should moisten light wool in tempered oil heated or in rose oil, and place it around the joints, and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if he feels pain or putrefaction in the bowels, and it often happens, then cleanse them with warm black wine, and especially if the putrefaction extends to the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it from the inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small intestine.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeun" cannot heal when they are wounded, and this is due to the abundance of veins that are there, and because of the delicacy of the entire body, and its closeness in nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	and if the bladder jumps out of the wound, then put it back as you would with an intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and has turned green or black, then you must tie the place that is black so no bleeding occurs, for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut what is between the ligament, and let the two shoulders hang from the part below the wound up to above to lighten the extraction when the arrow falls, and the wound draws.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, for I have seen that one man was wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it became stitched and turned into a fistula, and through it came out excretions and wind;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to care for it until he was healed, and the wound was closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it sutured, I feared that the patient might have harm in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experimenter said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in such manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take fronds with large heads, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the frond has opened its mouth, place it on the two edges so that it presses its mouth upon them;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cut off the head, and it will stay so that it cannot untie, then place another frond after in the same manner as before, until the wound is entirely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	and the head burns in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take the head of this intestinal thread that is very lean, and then tie to the head of this thread a fine linen thread tightly, then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and reset it in the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching of wounds is not far from according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the great intestines, then there is no skill or health without subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	about the fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it awakens, is generally called a "fistula," and especially when it is hairy and discharges pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the truth a false knot hard and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also hairy like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes clear spittle, and other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and other times enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of this in the section on wounds, that any wound which is not healed and has no flesh, it cannot be except by one of the nine causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the insufficiency of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or by its maliciousness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	For there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, where no new flesh grows;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	where there is too much bile;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	where the pus is thin, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	where the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	where the corruption is of a pestilent nature;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	where due to the property of the region, digestion is slow, and health is delayed, and swelling occurs naturally;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones;
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I must make you know the treatment of fistula which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that occur in the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or on the skin, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and there is one that comes to the principal part of the member and similar areas.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is only labor and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is any fistula that does not reach the place I have mentioned, and you are confident in the treatment, and you want to understand it, take a probe of bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, then use it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is curved, then search it with a flexible probe of lead, for lead can bend around the curvature;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot search it well with probes, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for the moisture will flow from one opening to another, and cleanse it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then carefully probe it as much as you can, so that you may know if there is bone or nerve, and this is done properly, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when pressed by your hand, and the place where they feel it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the foulness and the corrupted matter that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep in a straight place, then you must cut deeply as much as you can, then put moistened tents with medicinal herbs inside, and push them to the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then apply healing ointments to grow healthy flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it off.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If vein or sinew does not bother the principal limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackening, then scrape it until all the corruption is removed, then treat it with things that heal flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not healed, and pus returns as before, know that you have not gone to the root of the problem:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	so expose and scrape until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the area;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if he is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	if not, know that the corruption is too advanced, that you cannot come near;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	there is no other method than to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small corrupted bone and you can extract it with tongs, then pull it out with the appropriate instrument for that, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, do not leave even one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture hinders you, and there is no mistake nor fear, then cut away both the moisture and the flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place on the wound something encouraging putrefaction, and leave until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then the bones will come out more easily;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh, then raise the putrefaction only until all the blackness is removed, then heal the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the corrupted area, it will reach the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	one must scrape and cut all the way to the putrefaction, and then treat it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you of an ulcer that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	The young man was about thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came within the body, so that the matter came to the leg, and it swelled with a large abscess, and he had no reason to defer opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the physicians by their folly worked so much on it that the abscess opened, and they let out a great deal of matter, and it became a fistula, and there came many openings that all discharged pus and moisture from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many physicians applied treatments for about two years, and there was no wise person in the art of hands until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medications with which he was being treated, and what discharged through the openings had a strong odor;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man would become red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I put up a tent in one of these perforations, and then searched all the perforations, and found that one came opposite the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I hurried then, and cut into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption reached to the inner bone;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I scraped what appeared to be the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption except that which I removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to treat the wound with poultices for a long time, and it could not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I began again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and scraped it, and then removed it, and attempted to heal the area;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not cut around more than a palm's width of the bone, and I pulled it out with all its flesh, then I restored it with medicines;
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and he was healed and stitched quickly, and there was no need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation he often bled, but was entirely healed, and in place of the bone a hard flesh grew, and it was well positioned and had no harmful or adverse effect whatsoever, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	and if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take the linen, and stretch it at the head of the exposed bone, and instruct someone to stretch it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and take another linen string thicker than the first one, and tie it on the flesh that is over the bone, and stretch the top end so that you pull the corrupted flesh underneath, and expose the flesh where you wish to sew, so that the suture does not bruise the flesh;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put the ember on a board under the bone to cut away the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and one must scrape as much as can be seen and felt of the corruption, and scrape again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover all the flesh;
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then put the ember underneath, and then scrape from one part to another the corruption, and let the scraper follow the length of the corruption closely, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut away the corrupted joint, and scrape the bone where it contains from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuity of the two joints, there is no other remedy but to cut;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or the ankle of the foot, it is a very serious matter, but nevertheless you must inquire about that corruption, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way that you can, but do not let the vein or the nerve oppose you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the incisors and the saws for cutting these bones are various, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and their fineness, and their size and their smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason, it is necessary to prepare his instrument for each kind of work;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work will show you the instrument you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the methods of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so consider the instrument you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	from the fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The joints become diseased either due to internal causes or due to external causes;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have treated that corruption with the care of medicines and they do not help, it is necessary to amputate that limb up to the place where the corruption comes from, so that the patient escapes death by this means or by the evil, which is greater, of the loss of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the sign is that the limb becomes black, so that it seems to be burned by fire, and after the blackness could come the corrosion member by member, and takes over the whole body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	and if you hurry to cut, and if it is due to the sting of venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and basilisk and the like, if the corrosion is at the head of the toe, then cut it off, and do not give space for it to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	and if it reaches the hand, cut it off at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, then cut it off at the elbow;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the knife, it is death, and there is no remedy other than the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and do the same when the corrosion comes to the stone:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes to the first joint, then cut after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the stone, then cut away the entire stone;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises up the leg, then cut at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy but to let the patient die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the method of cutting or sawing the limb is that you tie above and below, and stretch one minister at one end down, and another minister the other end up, and you separate the flesh which is between the two ties to a span wide, until the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then you cut or saw, and place on each side a cloth of linen, so that the saw does not touch the healthy area, and does not cause another injury and heated abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	and if bleeding occurs when you operate, then quickly cauterize the area, or apply some binding powders;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your treatment until it is completed, then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it heals;
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to the man in such need:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	a darkness befell him that seemed like the burning of fire, and that corruption came first to his toe of the foot, until it would spread over the entire foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he hurried to cut off the foot, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and a long time after, the corruption returned to his toe of the hand, and he came to me, and I applied repellent things after cleansing the body, but the corruptions could not be stopped;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, as I had hope of repelling the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also doubted that if I cut his hand, he would die, for the strength of the man was weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he completely despaired, and returned to his land, and hurried to cut his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not found content elsewhere except for what is done differently when it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes in the cartilage, and remains for so long that it forms a large collection of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it rots and bursts, and the pus comes out, and the hole remains there for a long time, like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin that is above is as delicate as fine draperies, and does not extend down to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy," and is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so extended that it reaches the bone entirely, it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is such that you cut that skin all around, especially when it is delicate, just like fine draperies;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not matter because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you fear that the skin will burn, and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with aclyster thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Look if the breast is large, and the milk that comes out has a foul smell, then cleanse it with Egyptian medicine which is made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take arsenic, and oil, and white lead, equally, and put to cook in a vessel over fire, until the medicine turns red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and cleanse the breast with it, and bind the wound;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine on for two hours, then remove it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times until the breast is cleansed and the stench is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and sometimes it isclysterized with ash water, when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes of vine wood, and throw water over, then strain it, and use it as a clister until you know that the intestines are well cleansed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot tolerate it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water, thenclysterize him with water and honey in which there is a bit of ground litharge;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you clysterize it with honey and mixed wine, for the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine causes the body to heat;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you are confident that the intestines are well cleansed, then clysterize him with what causes flesh to grow in them, and it is that you take a diaphoretic plaster, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	where you cleanse with some medicines and ointments, of which I have described the properties in the treatment of ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the opening of the breast is small, and the nozzle of theclyster cannot enter, then widen it with an iron a bit, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too wide, sew it up leaving only enough space for theclyster to enter, and if the opening that expels pus is at the top, cut it lower where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the pus is perfect, do not let any foreign matter enter;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cut the breast below as you wish, then arrange in such a way that the bow goes to the lowest place there is, for when the bow is fully formed, it does not allow any flesh to enter and if you cannot cut the breast below as you wish, then prepare in such a manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	that the bow moves lightly downward, and leaves nothing of the bow;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidative medicines to put on the wound, and stretch over the linen cloth that covers the entire wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cut at the strong place the opening of the breast a bit wider than the first, then spread an ointment over another cloth according to the size of the opening, and put it on the wound's opening to alleviate the bow, and do not remove the large cloth except once after many days;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and the one who is on the nipple of the breast, often removes it to remove the pus, and you know what comes from the pus, whether it is venom or blood or enough, or digestible, or indigestible;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take notice if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a manner and you see that nature rises up on the nipple of the sore, then know that the breast is already curing, and health approaches;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other bandage, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast expels undigested phlegm after many days, know that the breast will not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle pus forms after a long time, do not despair of the health, for recovery approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are people who take too long to remove the flesh from their wounds, and of those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested milk spits from the breast after many days, know that the breast does not heal;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breast is slow to heal and is swollen, apply drying but moist in substance and dry in virtue medicines, such as diaphoretic ointment, for it has a large part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diaphoretic ointment, and make it with rose oil, and sprinkle it with old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	then cook it and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and this same is best when the diaphoretic ointment is not available, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it over the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then in glue the cloth, and stretch it over the breast, and sometimes one administers aristologe longe, and roots of celestial lily, which is also like flour of veal and centaure.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and use simples or compounds:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	grind them, and make powder, and put on the honey that I have said, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment, then know that the corruption is perfected, and makes an impression in the bone, or in the hard members, or in the ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	treat the fistula as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarice is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the little finger of the hand, or of the foot, or perhaps arises in other fingers;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it grows old, and no attention is given to it, then comes the hot abscess, and it runs and throws pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps it corrodes it entirely;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corrosion reaches the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the joint of the finger becomes swollen, and its color turns purple.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut off with an iron all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is greatly helpful if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail presses against the flesh inside and begins to pierce it, and injures it, then you should place a thin piece of iron under the nail that pierces the flesh, lift it up, and cut away that flesh subtly and lightly, and apply burning and corrosive medicines on the remaining flesh to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with ointments until he is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it away and draw out, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the toe becoming corrupted, cut it as it is said before, then treat it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is bitten, and swollen, and he feels great pain, then you must cleanse it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the nail of the infected area sharply by cutting across it, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the swelling of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The dislocation that occurs in some men's hands is entirely fleshy, and sometimes it has bones, and occasionally there is a nail, and some are born at the root of the joint, or the origin is in some parts of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	He who is born with any knot on the toe does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the toe, by chance moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of he who is fleshy is light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	He who is born in the root of the joint is difficult to treat:
si te tien dou coper.	be careful with cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In him who is born with an anus or should have it at the back, you must first cut the flesh roundly to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable seam for this, then clean it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The web that comes on the fingers together comes by birth, or by wound healing, or by fire burn, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	you must cut that suture so that the toes return to their natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two tents or cloths moistened with rose oil so they do not stick;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you place between two pieces of thin linen until the wound is sealed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If webbing comes on any of his fingers with the palm, then cut that webbing as appropriate.
des vils	of the villages
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large and wrapped full of melancholic superfluities, which come to many parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it happens more in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is then necessary that you administer to him a purgation of bile, and then heal him with basilicum.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The iron cure is according to two methods:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is that they are cut, and the black blood is drawn out;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other method is that you lift the vein, and draw it entirely out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The castration is according to this method:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	first raise the leg with very hot water until the thick part is made subtle, then remove the leg of the patient from above the thigh down to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then cut the vein in one place, or in two or three, with a wide incision, then lift and draw out the black blood forcefully from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the strength of the patient can endure;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it off, and instruct them to cleanse themselves with black bile-inducing foods;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and it is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The elevations of it are according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	shave the patient's leg if it has a lot of hair, then put it in the bath, and wash the leg with warm water until it becomes red, and the veins swell;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat it with fire, and then cut directly from the vein at the knee to the area below near the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then work the skin with the lancet, and strip the vein on both sides until it appears when you feel it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and when it is seen red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white thread;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then push the root underneath, until it is lifted from the skin, and then pierce it lightly with a lancet, then cut it in another place three times;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it with a thread, as you have done, and pierce it with another lancet, as you did first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then cut another section, or several if you need them, then lift it, and cut at the tip with your thumb, then pull and lift until the second section;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then extract it piece by piece until all of it comes out, then cut it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot pull it out, then put a needle with the thread doubly strong, and tie it and pull it, and insert it under the skin, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not break, for if it breaks, one cannot pull it out or lift it, and harm comes to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have pulled it all out, then put wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the site of the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the skin is tight and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not cut it off;
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the skin is curved, and it does not cut deeply, so that it does not cut the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of thick curvature, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil war
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is located in the legs, in warm areas where no herbs or trees grow, and in soil that has no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance it arises in another place than the legs, and this happens due to the putrefaction that comes under the skin, just as serpents and worms come within the body between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.
