And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a great inflammation comes to the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to come out forcefully, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the wound is open, you must wrap around a piece of linen from one and a half fingers up to two fingers wide, and tie it, and leave the linen hanging on the leg, and every time some comes off due to decay, wrap it around the linen again, and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root until it is entirely out;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it will re-enter the flesh and cause an abscess and putrefaction in that place, leading to a bad illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For this reason, it is necessary that it be treated little by little until the end, and nothing remains in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and sometimes this vein is treated when it is five palms long, or ten, and a man came to me once, whose was ten palms long, and when you cut it, you put one reed into the hole, and pierce until the bottom, so that everything comes out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and the material inside should be emptied out, and apply to the area medicines that prevent putrefaction for some days, then treat it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes this vein has fewer reeds, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or in the foot, and many holes come from it, and from which few reeds sprout;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Then cure it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land "cattle sickness," for it often occurs in cattle, and it is a small worm that lives between the skin and flesh, and moves all over the body up and down, and one can feel it well as it travels from member to member, until it bursts the skin where it goes, and becomes fierce;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is caused by putrefaction of certain humors, such as worms and snakes and earthworms and ascarids in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and there is fear of its maliciousness, for when it moves through the body and ascends to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance it may enter and destroy the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you want to treat and care for it, one cannot do so except when it comes.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then you must bind the area above and below with a strong tight bandage, then cut above and draw it out forcefully, and if the pus is embedded in the flesh and you do not find it, then cauterize with fire above until it burns;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is to corrupt the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye on the head, then press below it firmly on the eyebrow, then cut above and draw it out forcefully;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary to treat the patient with body cleansing of soluble medicines for the corrupt bad humors, and they should be fed nutritious foods to prevent corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she bared her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and it then rose up as quickly as a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, just like quicksilver when it moves from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departs from that place, and fixes in the shoulder, and then a bit after runs throughout the body, until it comes to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it turned around the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I had wanted to believe that it was good to move the pain from one place to another, but I had not wanted it, as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and the veins exposed, and because of this the constrained wind appeared;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear according to this reason in those who are plethoric, and who have moist bodies and veins hidden.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you wish to treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, then scrape above and below quickly, and then cut so that that wind constrained in place comes out;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the place;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat it with those that expel the winds, such as foul pills, and pills of serpent, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their forms and according to the places of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity among them is that there are those which have large points, and small ones, and branched ones, and soldered ones;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those which have pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and she who falls on any limb falls according to two manners:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in principal members it affects, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she falls then in any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then you must beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death follows in many cases;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not embedded deeply, then extract it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when an arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and the suture which is on top of the brain jumps, is when there is scotoma and bleeding and inversion and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasms and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perchance it comes out without force from the nostrils, or from the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and by chance loses the speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the wound jumps white moisture resembling pus, and it also jumps like broth of flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then be cautious with the treatment, and remove the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of pleurisy when it falls upon the heart are that it is near the left breast, and it feels as if it were fixed in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and sometimes the pleurisy beats like the pulse, and it causes black blood to come out, and coldness and cold sweat occur, and syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then you can be sure that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that remains in the body is that without pause foam jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks the cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow falls on the covering of the lung, it is near the lower ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and it causes great anguish and great pain and sighing;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and it moves all the limbs from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perchance some undigested flesh may jump from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and if any dung comes out through the intestines, there is no hope in the treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrowhead falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes to flow, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the arm and the spine and the wrist and the thigh and the legs, and similar members, are safe according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow struck him in the armpit at the root of the neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I probed it, and pulled it out from the other side beneath the ear fat, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And in one attempt, I pulled out an arrow that had struck him in the eye fat beneath the eyelid, and the arrow was embedded, and I could not reach beyond the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was as large as a Turkish bow's iron part, almost light without feathers;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The eye was healed, and no adverse incidents occurred to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And he drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I shaved the beard, and worked carefully until I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I drew an arrow from the man, which had lodged in his abdomen, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, dislodged it, drew it out forcefully, and he had no adverse effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man to whom an arrow has fallen into the back, and the wound was sealed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural disposition, nor finds harm in any of its natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And you see another man to whom an arrow fell into his face, and the wound was sealed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and remained thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And extract an arrow from the man of the king's court, into whose nose the arrow had fallen, and it was slightly leaning to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat her after she had been fallen for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	And I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I wanted to examine her in a completely private tent, and did not feel any;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a prick and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I placed on the area a plaster that is attractive and digestive, so that the area would not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the head of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the plaster for several days, and reopened the wound again, and the patient remained this way for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his chest;
et il le me dist.	and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put corrosive medicine on the wound for several days until it opened, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow that was embedded in the place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I applied that corrosive medicine to the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow appeared visibly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it took about four months to complete the process around the wound, and then I widened the wound so that I could insert the forceps, and I moved it from one side to the other, but it could not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then I did not stop refining and devising methods of instruments until one day I grasped it with well-made forceps, according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, until I pulled it out and closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physician judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	Then I restored it, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you apply your care to what I do not mention, for the books cannot take everything into account;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the wise masters compare very little, and upon what is present and lacking, find new work and new instruments, through the understanding of foreign things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not remain in the members where they are embedded without two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and the one that jumps out where it enters is an arrow entering its flesh, and sometimes it jumps out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out now, leave it until the flesh around is rotten, and the discharge is diluted;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is embedded in the bone and cannot come out, leave it that way for some days and move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps out, and if it does not jump out, pierce around the entire shaft finely until the surrounding area is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the brain's chambers, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned become apparent to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	do not remove it, but leave it until it is equal after some days, for if the arrow comes up to the surface, it is deadly.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not fixed solely in the bone and does not reach to the surface, and the patient remains for some days without ill effect, then the instrument should be used to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out easily, then apply tar around it, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then clean the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is embedded in a part of the body where it cannot be seen, seek it throughout the entire area;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it with a suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then cut it so that the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and pull the arrow if you can, and if it has ears by which it is held, then remove the flesh that is embedded from two parts as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful that you do not break the arrow, so that you can pull it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then leave it until the area around is swollen, then pull it out, for the extraction will be eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood is contrary to you, then administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of the incision of the nerve and the vein, and devise how you can draw out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient according to the position they were in when the arrow struck them, for this is the greatest help there can be, and if you cannot, then place them according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, or where some part of it is visible, or the skin is swollen in such a way that it can be seen or felt clearly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Cut then up, until the forceps can grasp, and then extract:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it is now possible.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then rotate your hand roundly, until it enters into the bone, and widen the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it again, and then restart the extraction until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the shaft of the arrow is there, push it with the entire shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the shaft breaks off and you wish to administer further, then use the instrument with hair, so that the tip of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then push out; and if the arrow is barbed, use the pointed instrument to enter it, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, then you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then clean the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls on the hip or in the abdomen or at the bladder or at the side, and it is close, and you can cut over it;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of cutting the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the pincers used to pull out arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and you see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many methods:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form of the hair tip is also like the feather of a bird, to place at the tip of the arrow, as shown here the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tongs for piercing and pressing is here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	the veins of the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are thirty-one veins from which one recovers, of which sixteen are in the head, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	The flaps that are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two glands that are in the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the upper lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins from which we commonly bleed are 5 in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and the common people call it the "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "faste," and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and the common people call it the "vein of the heart";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic is on the right side, and the common people call it the "vein of the belly," and it is on the forearm, and it is the one from which we bleed, which appears clearly on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the saver vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is below the corbeure of the instep on the left side, and the second is the sophene which is at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein which is called "nesse", which is at the ankle on the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The inflammation of the veins that are behind the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of the surgeon, as I tell you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then have the patient compress his neck with a twist, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	take them then in your hand, and where you feel the pulse beneath your hand, mark it there;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet, and pierce below the vein until the bone, then lift your hand along the entire vein above, and cut both the skin and the vein well twice across, and let the blood flow out as much as you wish;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then extract and bind until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said about the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The inflammation of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for old migraines, soreness, and customary ophthalmia, and for watery tears in the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the inflamed are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient stretches his neck so that the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse under your thumb, and then sign from there;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lift the vein with your index finger and place the lancet underneath, and lift the vein up, and cut it, just as you have done in two other veins, and let the blood according to your necessity;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then tie it firmly, and leave it until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have already spoken of their cutting and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The vein of the forehead is as useful as the cephalic vein for old diseases of the face, and for migraines, and for redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting until the veins appear;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "digging tool", of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the tip on the vein, and press down with your hand, or with something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you wish;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein so that it is sealed, and sometimes the work is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it is not right that the flames be too sharp;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and cut sideways, because the bone is near, and by chance the flame might break when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The swelling of the two veins that are in the two temples helps the eyes, and with the sty, and with redness, and with the sore in the eye, and with diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their swelling is that the patient strains his neck by twisting some ligament, as mentioned before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then it swells, and the swelling should be across, a bit long of the flame and a bit wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are fine, they may break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then let blood as much as you need, and then bind on cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The swelling of the vein of the nose is good for water, and for strong decoctions, and for illnesses of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, especially when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the swelling is that the patient tightens his neck, then pulls his nose with your left hand, and take the fine long flame, and insert it between the two nostrils in the space that is there, for the vein does not open well on its own, and the pus will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and let blood according to your need, then leave it for a night, for it is restored very quickly;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The salve of two binders helps with the tightness of the collar, and at the beginning of mixing, and with many diseases, and with ringworm, and with corrosives, and with herpes, and warts;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the salve is that the patient pulls his neck under one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the master be standing on the head of the patient, and the patient sits on the chair, then apply the salve to the vein widely, then draw blood moderately, as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then do the same on the other vein, then loosen the ligature, and moderately constrict the veins so that the patient does not strangle;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave it until morning, when the wound should be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the swelling of the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The swelling of the veins of the upper lips helps with phlegm in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and cracks in the lips, and from the nose and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bleeding is to sit the patient in front of you, and constrict his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are recognized by their black color, and by the small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	cut both of them, and if you do not recognize them and are in doubt, then cut the largest one on each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the swelling under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The swelling of the veins under the tongue helps after the swelling of the cephalic vein, and this is at the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the swelling is that the patient sits between your hands facing the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks underneath on each side a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	swell then one and the other, and do not go too deep, for underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the body that are commonly swollen are treated according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by pricking with an entire martian flask, or with subtle olive oil like cutting bodies, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The first form of the martian flame is much renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	and it is necessary to open the full and closed veins filled with thick visible blood, which contain thick and murky blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more finely pointed, and it is for healing the fine veins where there is fine citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed wisely and to be careful of the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	and if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, then he must stop it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the flames should not be pricking but cutting like a file.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	and if the basilica does not open clearly, you must extract it and change to another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or if you want any vein of it, or you incise in its place the vein along the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the edge of the flame should be file-like, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	and if you wish to know the place of the incision, you must first extract the arm, touch the place until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place of the joint, then bind the arm, and cut the vein from the flame inward;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and be careful not to hit the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is from the artery:
eschui la donques.	avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it spurt up like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is the blood of the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then, and press your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	bind the arm, and leave it thus, and let the patient not move it;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be under fear, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the blood flow is not stopped, and it overwhelms you, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it appears, for the head of the retractors;
et estainche li sans.	and stop the blood flow.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	and take a bark of fig, and split it, and take one of the halves and bind it on well until the next day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if the blood is stopped, it is good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, then treat it as we have said, with powders that stop blood;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the bindings are not severe in many positions due to the small space of the wound, and the strength of the arm's joint.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein in the middle helps draw blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and the cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is necessary for the surgeon to be careful of the nerve that is below, and if he pierces too deeply, and he hits the nerve, it swells and the patient's health becomes severe, and perhaps cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve appears often, and if it does not appear in some people due to its subtlety, you must probe for it with the anesil instrument;
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and cleanse the nerve to your ability.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The application of the cephalic helps, drawing blood from the head, and aids the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to apply it by pricking with olive oil flame or myrtle flame, for it is the safest of all veins, for there is neither nerve nor artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, it is necessary to find the lightest spot, and it does not matter if one misses the first time, and one retries;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and sometimes the area swells for some people when one misses the first time, but it does not matter.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the sanie is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about medicine, is that medicine is not practiced merely to maintain health, and to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins that are in the arm;
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to know, cephalic, saphenous, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed at the beginning of spring in January, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The medicine that is administered to the illnesses has no determined time, but when there is need by day or night, at all hours and in every season;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not appropriate to bleed children until 14 years, nor a woman carrying a fetus from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	And one should not treat those who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner, it is necessary that they purge the intestines with a mild enema if they have much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines the harmful superfluities detrimental to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor should one bleed those who are overly satiated with food, nor those who are drunk until they recover, nor those who are dropsical;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one suffers from cleansing after colic pain, and vomiting, and diarrhea, and frequent intercourse with a woman, and work, of staying awake and fasting, and that which robs all strength, whether by weapon or body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then refine the humors, if the blood is thick, through foods and drinks and medications, if you have the power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to refine the blood, and let blood from the vein of the arm around the third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard yourself that day from work, and from piercing, and from lust, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be bound and joyful, and let the leeches be higher than those whom one bleeds, and rub the arm two times or three, then bind the bandage above moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, blood cannot flow;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell, and they can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then moisten the leeches with a little old oil, then place his finger of the left hand on that vein below the area where he wants to bleed, so the vein does not move when pricked.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee like cords from the bleeder, and some are full of windiness, so when one places the flame upon them, they retract from the flame, and one cannot open the vein, and thus one is of those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he works the vein, the wound is too narrow, for this reason the surgeon must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein is worked the first time, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then begin again a little below that place or above quickly, if the area is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is swollen and the patient is frightened, leave it for one day or two, and do not loosen the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	perchance hot abscesses may come;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter the bath, then restart the surgery if it pleases you;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the blood comes out subtly and you fear that not enough blood will come out as you wish, then cauterize that opening entirely with the flame directly;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and perform it somewhat hastily, so that the area becomes swollen;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area swollen, do not begin the bleeding again, and put on a bit of oil residue, for it lightens the body from blood, and in this place, the residue is milder than the oil;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil residue in each bleeding that you bleed the veins to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this same thing makes a trilication and applies egg white when it is placed upon the site;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	so refine the sinew and split it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, especially when it is not sufficiently opened at the time when the vein's opening is small, then hurry and place on the site a sponge moistened in warm water and salt for a little while, and bind it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if there remains any blackness or greenness at the site after some days, it does no harm;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you wish, put on some substance of aloe or of myrrh mixed in juice of calamus, mastic, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often an abscess and appearance occur in the swelling of the basilic vein:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	put your hand on it, and if you find the spot soft to the pressure of the hand, then that appearance is malignant.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Therefore, avoid putting on any of those things we have mentioned, for fear it might cut into the artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but make for it a dry poultice to harden the spot, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each the blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and of the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it thick, let it flow until it is thinned;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for those who are full and strong, and need bloodletting, that a larger wound be made, and the flames be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to let blood less and more frequently, and it should be done by cutting across, not by piercing;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of bloodletting is safe from bleeding and nerve damage, and is better than long or wide bloodletting.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And to those whose body is lacking at the healing, it is necessary to give moist bread in pomegranate juice;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If it is heated, then bleed three or four times. And if it is of a cold temperament, then before the healing, eat moist bread in musk syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and strongly scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints from the bleeding, after the discharge of much blood, then it is necessary that he inhales a broth of meat and a subtle aromatic syrup, and uses the other things we have mentioned in the section or chapter on syncope for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bleed one arm and bleed another time, then it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleeds a little at a time, according to the amount of his continuous strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to bleed one arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, then he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to be bled from the other side, should be bled on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood within the body that is already heated, and it causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	so it is necessary to bleed a large quantity and widen the opening until it flows into the basin;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you should examine all the signs of healing, and place your hand on their pulse when they heal, so death does not come instead of health, and this happens often, when the healers are negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not appropriate when you want to release the arm and make blood come out a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press strongly on;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is swollen, should he extend the arm hastily, for that would be harmful;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but leave it until it heals a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you poke with the tip of the flame until the blood that is clotted in the wound comes out, and place on it a piece of cloth soaked in water, and press lightly on.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, then leave it alone and do not constrict it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is need to bleed for the second time, then bleed in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein inside the arm is bled instead of the vein of the head because it is composed that way.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of the salve is that the patient puts his hand in hot water, until the foscile is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be moderately bound, so that the vein appears well, then apply the salve across, not lengthwise or widthwise;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the opening be wide, and apply the salve close to the joint of the hand, and if nothing can come out, then put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is summer, do not put the hand in hot water, for it is used more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the inflammation of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The inflammation of the vein on the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	stretch out the hand, and put it in hot water until the vein is swollen, so that one can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the inflammation is across, and if you cut it completely through, it will cause no harm;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not go too deep, for the nerves are beneath entirely bare of flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as is necessary, put oil and seal on the vein to quickly close it, and do this for each cut.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The salve on the left hand is good for the disease of the spleen, and do everything as I have said for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of sophene is worth for all the diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the kidneys, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of its treatment is that the patient puts their foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it breaks, and binds over the joint of the foot;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and above it, many veins go up over the foot;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	treat then at the widest vein, or at the ankle, whichever is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you treat it on the foot, beware of the nerves beneath, and treat it crosswise as in cutting;
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flame be mild.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and let the vein fully empty.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	and if the treatment fails the first time, start again a little higher the second time, for the place is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and thus do with the splint of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The area of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its bleeding relieves the pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of its healing is that the patient enters the bath and tightens above the ankle four times by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then heal it in every way that you can, and by crossing;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is worth moving so that you cut it, for the pain is slight, and it is very beneficial to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then heal any vein that opens on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and let so much blood flow as you wish, and then loosen the tie, and put on cotton and bind it tight;
ele est maintenant sanee.	she is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of cupping treatments
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Leeches are made of horns, or of clay, or of glass;  
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and windiness is done according to two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by beating and drawing blood, or without beating.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this windiness which is without beating is according to two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or it is done with full fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and windiness which is done by beating and extraction of blood is done in fourteen places of the body, of which one is at the very top of the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and another is in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others on both sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suction under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suction on both shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction on the buttocks;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the suction cups on both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the suction cups on both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the suction cups on both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the ventosation does not draw any blood, for it acts on the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore does not weaken anyone, as is done with vein bleeding;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, neither in full heat nor partial heat, in any disease that comes from excess, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of diseases it is needed to cup, or for customs, then we perform it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at any time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they need to be cupped, have heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darkness before their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and spit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are those who dream and see blood and wounds and dead and similar things by night.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we order it to be bled after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The salve of hellebore helps with the dryness of the head… which affects the eyes, and it is not advisable to use this after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And this ventilation is in place of the salve of the cephalic, and it is not advisable for those with a cold disposition to use it, or those who have catarrh, for it does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for that reason, it is not advisable for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold diseases in the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often recover from it become forgetful, and for this reason, the cupping should be placed a bit lower due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Ventosation around the neck is in place of the salve for the head and the basilica, and for that reason, it is useful for constriction of the breast, and to split the channel of the nostril, and for all, and for fullness;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and there must be a little pressing, for if it holds too tightly, it engenders faintness or nausea in the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	Wind in the two ribs of the neck is good for headaches, and opthalmia and migraine, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the sanies of the basilic;
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and you must instruct the surgeon to press his hand when applying it, so that he does not cut the artery, and there are no flows of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	Wind beneath the chin is good for mouth diseases, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is in the place of the salves of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Windings on the shoulders are good for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The ventilation of the guts is worth as much as the three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instructs the surgeon not to incise too deeply, for the muscle is bare of flesh, and lies beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping that is on the buttocks is worth for hemorrhoids of the anus, and for diseases beneath, and it is necessary that the cupping be large, and be of glass, so it can draw well;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if they were delicate, they would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and I make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The leg cupping treatments are very effective, for they draw blood from the entire body, and they are useful for old pains in the reins, and of the spleen, and of the bladder, and repeatedly alleviate the flows.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are placed at the sites of the two ankles, and the two heels, and over time they weaken the body with long use, and cause fainting in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The method of applying the cupping is that you first place it empty, suck moderately, apply quickly, move evenly, and do not stop until you see the area turn red and swollen, and then release the blood's redness;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then apply force, and reset the cupping devices, and take care in the positioning of the body, for there are those who have so much flesh, and clearly poor:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	so it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and one deep incision;
et suce legierement.	and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the vein is large, then it is necessary to strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to refine the path of the thick blood.
