Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, then it is necessary to strike a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw blood little by little, then we strike only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we wish to let much blood, then we often reopen;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, then use a sharp instrument, and it is important that the veins be punctured suddenly, and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the places of the cupping with opening and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in this state, of violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in ivory, of watercress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or other similar oils.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, then take oil of marjoram, or of balsamite, or oil of aniseed, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one to be treated has tender flesh and large pores, then no oil should be applied, but it is necessary to wash after ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or water of black nightshade, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who have much moisture, it is lifted with oil of ash, or water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large excesses rise from old wine, or from juice of succory, or from decoction of anise or chamomile, or from other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it is not suitable to bleed with cupping before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath one hour or two;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and do not sleep after the cupping, and it is necessary that he sweats, when he should be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware if the one who is bleeding is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	it is necessary that he takes cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces with garlic, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and soft porridges, and castrated fowl meat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold temperament, let him take honey syrup, and moderately scented wine, which is between old and new, and soft foods, and soft porridges and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day he will be cupped, he should drink more than he eats;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some people at times treacle or nutmeg before cupping, or after, to strengthen the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the broth be refined, but it is not suitable for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The suction cups that are placed without striking are those that are placed upon the liver, and upon the spleen, and gout, and upon the abdomen and the buttocks and the kidneys and the hip, for these limbs do not endure being struck upon them, and it is done only to draw blood from limb to limb, as we place upon the breasts when the child suckles;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity which is in the limb, as we place suction cups upon the abdomen and upon the buttocks to reduce the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain when there is an obstruction or stone, so by its attractive power it may possibly remove the obstruction, or dislodge the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and thus it does when placed upon the liver and upon the spleen when there is retained wind, and these cupping vessels are administered empty to suck solely;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes are administered together fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a manner that one fills the cupping vessel with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two fingers in width and half a palm in depth, and it has on the side around the middle one small hole, as if to insert a needle, and it should be made of brass, smooth so that it does not injure the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and have in the middle a crossbar of brass or iron, to hold a torch tightly, and let them be both large and small according to the illnesses and age of those who use them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suction cups for children are different from those for the elderly, and for the thin different from those for the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should place this suction cup on the limb in this way:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the wax torch or the linen strip, and place it inside the suction cup across the bar that is inside the suction cup, so that the flame is at the bottom of the suction cup so it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and your fingers should be on the opening we mentioned, so that when you want to, the vapor escapes, and you remove the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and imprint the liniment as before, and repeat it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping which is administered for a disease of pleurisy, to all water, there is no vein or pore, and it is not administered except when it is full of water, and is placed on the limb only briefly;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Blistering is only administered in areas where cupping cannot be applied due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on areas bare of flesh, such as toes or nails, and other similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the use is such that when you find veins that are in clear sweet waters without putrefaction, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place one nut in sweet water, until they become familiar, and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then let it be bled with a vein and a cupping glass, then rub the limb until it is red, and place on the veins;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and fall out, if it is a place where you can apply a cupping glass, then apply it, for it helps greatly afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then clean the area with ash, and then with water, very well, and then stamp it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the wound is too far from the body of the veins, then moisten the linen cloth in cold water, and place it on, until the blood is stopped;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the blood is multiplied, then place vitriol powder or gall, and similar things, until it is stopped;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the place half of peeled beans, and leave them until they burn at the site, it will stop now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, then take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and if the veins do not want to be taken, then rub the place with fresh blood, or you stick a needle until blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will burn;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they fall, sprinkle on a pot of aloes and crushed charcoal, or ash, so they will now fall.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the foolish physicians discard this chapter, which they have never seen in any of the ancient books, nor read a letter of it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason, the knowledge is rare in our land, for I have never found any good one;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of it except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the subject with knowledge, and by experience, and by the habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and have summarized at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are mentioned, as I have done in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the words and the chapters where the wise place their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or contusion comes to anyone, you must hurry to treat the patient on one side and the other, if nothing else prevents it, such as weakness of body, or fainting, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the weather is not very hot, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and eat cold foods, that is to say cold broths, and meat of chicken and veal, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overload yourself with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no fear of a hot abscess, or the spreading of matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	so the patient returns to his first government which he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with foods that promote thick nourishment, where there is viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and eggs, and meat, and cow's stomach, and poultry, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment the break mends and heals faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of old and frail people cannot be easily mended or united according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor can those which are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but have no concern, place on the broken bone the thick tendons which hold and join the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not stop all of his work, and for that reason he must be nourished with hearty meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manner of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that require elevation, and others in sharpening, such as the cutting of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small裂痕。为了保持翻译的准确性，最后一部分“fendure”更准确地译为“fissure”或“split”，因此句子可以调整为：“And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small fissure.” 但是根据您的要求，我将提供一个直译版本。
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And for each method have his ingenuity and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the memory comes into place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the bone fracture is recognized by the fact that the limb is twisted, and it is clearly visible due to deficiency, and it sounds under pressure from the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may well have twisting, or splitting, or small fractures.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you must not move it by hand, but apply medicines that come after here, and then hold it tightly now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that for fractures that go outward, and the two parts are separated, they must now be put evenly in place, although abscesses may come;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if hot abscesses come, leave it for some days until the abscesses are calmed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then set it equal to the motion that you can do lightly and wisely, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of those in which there are pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then bind it, as is appropriate afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone has broken pieces, then stretch it in two parts, if it is a hand or foot, or with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two ropes, or with one rope and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb according to its natural form, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, you reset all the fragments in their places as much as you can, and be careful that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient;
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and properly align the two ends of the bone according to the best methods.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	and you can feel with your hand if it does not seem properly aligned:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	raise it gracefully, and do not pull too tightly, nor press as those who cause a hot abscess and contraction in the limb through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is properly set, instruct the patient well that they do not move it, whether awake or asleep, or turning, or in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and ensure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, it is not complete, and it must be put into such a position that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is put straight, so no twisting comes when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and the like:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	one must wrap cloths of soft and fine linen;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as thighs and shins:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	one must wrap with a broad and hard binding, for the wide bindings embrace the entire large limb and constrain it equally on all sides, so there is no unevenness;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then bind around with light bandages, three turns or four according to the limb, and tighten your hand a bit on all the binding, then go above the fracture and tighten less, so that the fracture may spread slightly apart;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the binding little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy area, then take another binding, and wrap around again over the fractured area;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part below the fracture, and tighten moderately, not too strongly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first line above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place between the bindings threads of linen or cloths, until it is all even, then bind everything on top with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place something soothing on the abscess that is warm and which reduces the swelling, and leave it this way for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then stretch over your stakes, and let them be half a large cane in width set firmly, or of wood from which we make cleats, or palm ribs, and let them be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the stake which one places on the break be a bit thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and it should also be as long as is necessary for the member's smallness or largeness;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then stretch over the stakes as you have done at the first place, then bind over a suitable thread, just as in the first place on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	narrower below, then less;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the threads be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and they should be of soft flax;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their ligatures from twisted linen cords, and it is great error, for the ligature cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not have less than a grain's space between each needle.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the heads of the arrows after they are embedded in their flesh, place beneath them tow of flax, or shredded wool, so that it does not harm.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splinter, and the skin is broken, I will speak of the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not right to extract arrows from all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, it is not necessary to place strong stitches that after five days or seven, or more according to your certainty of a hot abscess coming.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and see here the method of ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and twist:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take the flour that clings to the mill walls, and mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster restoring the fracture in various conditions, especially for women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of plaster restoring the fracture and the dislocation and the twist:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	take З pounds of balsam and labdanum and alum and asafetida and gum arabic and myrrh, in total X З.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	mirtle and aloe, each half an ounce;
alechil VIIII З.;	alochil nine halves;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make it into powder, and mix it with egg white;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the person's complexion is hot, then use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another kind of plaster that is good for sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take myrtle and vervain, each ten halves;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	mirtle and aloe, each nine halves;
acaice VI З.;	accident VI Z.; 
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Bole armeniac X З., and grind well, and cook with water or egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way of plaster for joints and bones dislocated from their places, and to ease the ensuing pain, and for bone fractures and breaks:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	take new wool, and boil it in oil, and apply it to the area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not heal, but they are good for soothing a hot abscess and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way of plaster that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	take dried fig leaves and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of malva, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of wych elm, one part of each;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander water, or with water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of making a stronger plaster than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of malva, and flaxseed, balustrum, melilot, and figwort, and flowers of violets and chamomile, one part of each;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not place on the broken limb to restore strength anything but a salve made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says it should be between two neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen thinks one should place on the broken limb, to restore, things somewhat dry and warm, such as myrrh and aloe and frankincense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another method for a plaster that is good for injuries and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mutton fat and human nails cut off, or bird feathers, and mallows, and salt equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and lay it on.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then loosen it a little after, and take care if the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	do not loosen it for several days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and loosen it, and remove the plaster now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and moist sea sponge, and soak it in water, and cleanse the area until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply dry wool soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it tightly until you are sure of a warm abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and rest the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then begin a gentle binding, and apply a poultice, and do not bind it as tightly as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat gently until he is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swelling has entirely been removed, and you need plaster and bandaging, then restart it as you did first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	and if none of what we have said applies to the limb, do not loosen it until after three days or four or five or seven;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what is seen, until the fracture heals, and the flesh grows over the alignment;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then he restrains it more than before, and swells his flesh, as I have said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the area dry more than necessary, know that no growth can come;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	apply then warm water, every time you release it, and this should be done every third day, and slightly remove the dressing;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this work then the growth returns to the limb, and quickly amends what the foolish doctors do, who restore the limb incorrectly:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it is harmful, and the work is fearful, and I see nothing else but to leave it alone and treat it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various kinds of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many kinds of fractures are there, and diverse shapes, and the causes are distinct;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures that are caused by the impact of a sword, and the collarbone removes all the bone down to the surface which is beneath the bone, just as an axe does to wood;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for that reason, this kind of fracture is called "hatchet wound.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	when the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and the wounds from these two fractures are large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded impact, or a split from the edge of a stone, or from falling on a stone, or from other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which approaches up to the tissue that is under the bone, or on top of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	and there is a wound that penetrates the bone as fine as a hair, and the split is small, and for that reason, this fracture is called "hairline";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound that is made by striking a stone, or by falling, or by similar things, and makes the piece of the bone go inwards, and the joint is twisted as do the blacksmiths when they strike on the cauldrons;
si entre li piere dedens.	and the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their head, such as a child's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all these manners of fracture that small pieces are separated as stars;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the incision on them, and by probing attempts, and by the corrupted flesh that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairline fracture is known by this, that when the bone is exposed and rubbed upon, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, be wary of the patient's accidents, and if you see any bad signs, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, stiffness, fainting, fever ague, and eyes protruding and reddening, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any astonishing accidents, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at least that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then you must hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the tissue under the bone be corrupted, and the accidents that we have mentioned come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	and if the bone fracture extends to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part thus:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and it is that you take the head of the wounded patient, and uncover on the bone in all ways that you can, and on the surface of the wound more than you can, and if bleeding comes from uncovering the bone, or an abscess hot, aid with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with cloths soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the hot abscess is calmed, and be sure of the bleeding;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to remove around the bone, and it is done according to two methods of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one method is that you cut with a narrow incision in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he makes another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is that you have a number of various cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and they are made of iron;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work lightly, so you do not bruise the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and strong, then you must pierce around it, otherwise you administer cuts with probes, not fully piercing through the skull bone, and the tip should have a margin or a circle that prevents the point from going through the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you must have several, so that each comes into its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have probes for all skulls;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and these are the forms of the three types of tarers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	and the quality to pierce around the broken bone is that you place one tarer on the bone, and turn with your hands until you know that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then place the tarer in another part a little afterward, and thus do all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and gently, as we have said, until you draw out the bone by hand, or with any of the instruments that you have such as forceps, pincers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and be careful not to touch the brain or the surface.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone and pulled it out, then you must remove the residue that remains in the bone with another instrument similar to an incisor, but it must be more slender and finer than other incisors;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if any of the small bones or scales remain, then remove them lightly with the instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then clean the wound with lint and ointments that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another method of practice is the one that Galen said, which is more thorough;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and he praises it greatly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first uncover a part of the bone where the fracture appears displaced, so that once you have uncovered this part, you will place under the head of this lens-shaped incisor, of which this is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, and the part is split on two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small mallet so that you lightly cut around the bone entirely, and be careful of the cloth that is beneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is adhered to the bone, remove it lightly, for it can be removed without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is cut only on top, and there are small pieces, then you must restore that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine scraper of which you should have various sizes, to apply in each place most suitably, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	And scrape first with large scrapers, and then with finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other haircuts and subtle fractures, you must administer treatment according to its direction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that is not unknown to one who has devoted their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the surface is exposed, then you must take a piece of linen, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another piece of linen doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first piece of linen;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as gently as you can so that you do not burden the surface, then apply another layer on top, and do not bind it too tightly but only enough for it to cover the wound;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it like this for one or two days until the hot abscess is calmed, then untie it, and apply medications such as lily roots, and powdered beans, and frankincense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and of these things make powder, and put on the wound, and immediately administer cleansing medicines without biting;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and ensure that the wound is immediately clean, do not leave any ointment, nor allow scabs to form, for when scabs form on the membrane of the brain, they can corrupt and harm it, causing great mischief to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when you put something biting on the surface, it burns above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackening does not come except from the medicine that you have put on, which has such power, then you should take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and glue one bandage, and put it on the surface;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with appropriate treatments until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes both parts of the nose above are broken, or one by itself, for there are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, so it does not cause to sink in or twist, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should put your little finger into the nostril hole, and place that break inside with your index finger, and push it back by force, until the nose returns to its natural form;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is on the upper part of the nose, and your fingers cannot reach the place, then you must put it equal at the head of a rod a bit thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, do likewise, and hasten to restore on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	and if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the hot abscess is calmed, then place at the head of the nail strips of linen cloth, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Place one other on the other side, if the break is there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the strips be so thick that they fill the gaps of the nail.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some say that one should moisten the threads with butter and change them each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem right to me, but they should be moistened in a mixture of egg white and mill powder;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the tent until the bone is hard, and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes one puts goose feathers in place of tents, and wraps a covering around it, and the breaker holds it, and the patient blows through;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or do what you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if hot abscesses come to the neck while you are working there, then put a poultice or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in a vial of diachylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if hot abscesses do not come, then apply a plaster made by mixing flaxseed flour and frankincense powder with egg white, then put light bandages on top, and do not bind the neck;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the neck fracture is small and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it with appropriate instruments, then sew up the tear, and treat it with things that heal flesh and promote healing, such as plasters and suitable ointments;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat it with tents, and put in rushes of pine until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured below, and there is no open wound, and the fracture is only superficial, and it is not broken into two, but rather indented inward, then it is recognized as slight.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the break is in the right part, that you put your index finger in the mouth of the patient;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the break is in the left jaw, then put your index finger of the right hand, and push the break inside gently, and tighten it with the other hand by force, and make it equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is separated into two, then you must administer extension from two parts until they are aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if movement of the teeth occurs or a tear, then extract them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then put on the broken jaw a cerate, and place a double cloth over it;
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and put on the cloth a large well-made needle, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it up as high as you can at the cheek, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	and if you see that the face changes, then untie it on the third day, and then reset what has changed;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and put a poultice on, of the mill powder with egg white or sesame flour, after you have removed the plaster;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put on the poultice a light wool, and if the poultices dry out and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it until he is healed;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	many times is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses come, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a break and wound together, bind if no piece of the bone has been removed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	so delicately remove the fragments with suitable instruments for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with fire according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, sew the wound if it is wide, and apply appropriate poultices to it to promote flesh growth until it heals.
de la forcele	about the fracture
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The forearm breaks often in front, towards the shoulder, and the break is according to three manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or it is broken and separated into two, and there are fragments, and it is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is when the break is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the forearm is broken;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then place the fracture evenly in your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or misalignment.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to stretch further, place under the patient's shoulder a round ball of cloth, or wool, and let it be large according to your necessity;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and stretch and lift the arm, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you set the fracture evenly as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder back into place due to it being stuck, then the patient must lie frequently on his side, and put a medium pillow under the shoulder, and the assistant pushes the shoulder down until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	and then align the fracture with your hands, and if you find it shattered, you must split it open;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and draw out the fragments gently, and if the bone cannot join due to some obstruction, then cut it with one of the incisors that you have;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but place under the forceps this instrument, to protect the surface:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it resembles a spoon, and is not closed, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and let it have two ends, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, as is the tear of the wound that you made when you drew out the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are sure of a hot abscess, cut the wound open, and if the tear is small, or if you doubt it is a hot abscess, then apply cloths and bandages to the wound according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, moisten the cloth with rose oil and ash and wine, and apply on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The compression of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you place on the bone the plaster of the powder from the mill and egg white, and put light bandages on top, and place a sphere under the splint, if you need one;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very wide bandage of a palm in width, then put the doubled cloth on top of the bandages, and the plaster;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a narrow strip of three digits wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the ends of the bandage are hanging;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the strip on the fracture, and wrap the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy splint, and under the diseased splint;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and the reset of each part, and when you see that the plaster holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the needle does not move over the broken bone, reward it each day, and when the bindings loosen, restrain it;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under the mattress when he sleeps, to raise the shoulder up;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	thus lighten the fracture of the forearm by lowering the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless bad accidents occur, until twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then restart the plaster, if you see that it is needed, and bind it tightly and leave it so until it is restored;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored in more than twenty-eight days, and in less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It often happens that the shoulder is broken at its broad part or not in the middle, and one does not know it except by touching it;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	so set it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then apply flour from the mill with an egg white and light bandages, and place a double cloth over it;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then place a wide and thin splint slightly wider than the shoulder, and if beneath the splint there are gaps in any part of the shoulder, use flax bandages to fill those gaps so that the splint lies evenly;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then it is bound with a large bandage firmly, so that the splinter does not move from its place, and the binding is checked each day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time it softens, it is bound, and the splinter is placed back in its proper place if it has moved, and the patient lies on their side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in twenty days or twenty-five.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is completed, then untie it, and be sure, for it is not bone that moves easily out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone sticks out and points under the heart, cut above it, remove the bone, and do what we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to appease the abscess heat.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breast fracture
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks from weakness.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it hangs down below, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks strength, and coughs, and perhaps vomits blood, and the fracture site in the bone becomes apparent, and it can be well felt.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on his back, and you place a cushion between his shoulders, then press the shoulders, and align the ribs from both sides with your hands, and delicacy in placing equally in all manners as you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then place poultices and pads over the stake made subtly of salt, or another light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, and lay it on the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the bandage around the back, and bind it moderately, and loosen the bandage every hour, and if it becomes loose, then bind it again;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it needs to be untied because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and untie it, and remove the plaster, and address what has come in ways of treatments;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reapply the plaster, and keep it tight until it heals.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaking of the ribs occurs only in their thick parts behind the back, and at the head inward, and they do not bend except because they are slippery;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and one can feel it well upon examination with the hands.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you set the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a splint, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the breaking of the ribs is leaning inward, then the patient feels great pain and pricking, like from pleurisy, for the bone pricks the membrane;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and alembic with points, and soon it vomits great spitting of blood, and this is from severe illness, and the old ones have put much ingenuity into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that one must administer foods that swell the belly, to push the stone downward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not wish for hot abscesses to occur if they have not already appeared.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has occurred, then we heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some say that we put cupping glasses on the place to bleed thoroughly, and this seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	nevertheless, there is doubt that the cupping may not draw the excess to the spot due to the condition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that we should cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and place pads between the ribs to distribute the heat evenly, then treat it with the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the bone piercing the tissue, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to cut over the spot of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place an instrument underneath to protect the surface;
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must cut the bone, and pull lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if hot abscesses come, then put on cloths soaked in rose oil, and apply to the area;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the area as appropriate for an abscess, and let the patient lie on their side where it is needed until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes the neck bones are fractured, and it happens that they bend;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and likewise for the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you wish to know if they will be healed or not, then take note if you see his hands softened and swollen and numb, and cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when they are squeezed and pricked, know that the bone joint is saved, and that the patient will be cured if care is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you wish to know if he will be healed or not, then beware if the feet are softened, and if the signs are present which are in the hands, and on the back there is flatulence and involuntary emission;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And when it is treated on his stomach, there is involuntary emission.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and wants to saddle up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is mortal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	do not labor too much in his care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, then the condition is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that you bleed it if there is a hot abscess, then put on the spine rose oil or egg yolk oil until it is calmed;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then place one of the comforting and drying plasters on it and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on the part where he feels the pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone becomes disjointed, it is necessary to cut on the joint;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and remove the bone, then sew together the two edges of the wound if it is large, then treat it with an ointment to promote healing until he is healed;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the skull," put your pouched hand (left), and make it equal to the other hand as much as possible, then apply the plaster and the splint on top if needed;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then he binds it, and if there is loose bone, he cuts into it, removes it, and treats the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It rarely happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does happen, there is only a slight reduction at the top;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and it extends downward, inclines outward, and causes pain, swelling, and bruising at the site of the break for the patient.
