et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each two sticks have one rotating stick, on which the ropes turn, and in two rotations have two small sticks of one palm long, to rotate the drill;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the rope that is among the boards to the drill towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other drill, and each of the assistants turns his drill along the whole rope, and the master places the point evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, then place a drying poultice with an abundance of egg, and then the wads, and then the stake of a tablet three inches long, which should touch the site of the swelling and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a rope as we have said, and let the patient use subtle nourishment until they are healed;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	and if any thing comes at the end of health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the stone that we have mentioned before;
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	and sometimes a piece of linen is administered, and sometimes the appearance comes in the last vertebra of the back, and one thinks it is a dislocation;
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and it is the bone that protrudes, for which one should not be presumptuous:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	perchance it might bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that in the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only dislocations occur, and they do not happen as they do in other joints;
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	inside and outside, and in front and behind;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and more inside than elsewhere, and slightly dislocated in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its internal dislocation is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick knee appears more open than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee to the ground;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and the area that is nearby is swollen with an abscess and hot because the head of the thigh bone comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of those to whom it comes to decay, is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	and the signs of that which happens in front is that he extends his leg well according to the alignment;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	However, the knee does not bend without pain, and if one wants to make it go forward, it cannot move ahead, and it retains its urine, and the ankle swells, and when it goes, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of those to whom it happens behind is that they cannot straighten their knee nor bend it, and that leg is more bent than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the hip joint is in a lower position under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The remedies for this kind of dislocation are that you reward if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its position, there is no treatment;
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and it does not require any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is one of the four types of dislocation, you must hurry to return the joint, stretch it inside and outside, and move it right and left;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	per chance it will return, and does not need another treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare the instrument strongly, and stretch the leg firmly with two hands, or with one binding above the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and another minister extends his hand above in such a way that he places his hands beneath the bones, then tightly binds a strong bandage on the thigh;
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another holds the end of the bandage;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they stretch up and down all at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to the four types, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If not, then one must pay attention to its appearance.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is on the outer side, then you should lay the patient on his healthy side, then place the bandage at the root of the thigh, and the spot that is below the angle, then extend the bandage up towards the angle, and towards the kneecap;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	then have another assistant take his arms, and embrace the thick part of the diseased thigh, and stretch it outwards strongly:
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	it will return to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot bind it in this manner that we have said, then you must tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong bond above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the affected leg be stretched out twice as long as the other;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then let it be hung on top of a post, and let it be two arms' length off the ground;
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then command the minister to grasp the head of the thigh, and let another minister hang with the patient, who firmly grasps the thigh, for the joint now returns quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is severe, the patient lies down, as we have said in the case of one who has rheumatism, and bind the bandage tightly on the affected leg properly, and on the weight also;
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then put two brands, one at the head and the other at the feet, then place one brand between the thighs of the patient in the form;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have placed damp cloths around so that it does not hurt the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and the physician puts equal with his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put it on the table, and press it as we have said in gilbositeit, and lay the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the affected leg quickly, and according to what I have said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and the physician places his palm on the affected angle, then presses with the other hand, and stretches it down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is behind, it is not necessary to extend the patient downward, nor lift up onto the ground, but it should be as if the hip were dislocated behind, just as we have said about lying on the two hips;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and let it be on his face, and the bandage extended as we have said before, and one must press on the joint at the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and it will be right when the patient stretches his legs, and they will be equal;
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then align the thighs, apply the plaster, and strap with a bandage so that the hip does not move;
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and let him rest for three or four days, then loosen it, and apply the plaster again;
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are equal, then strap them as before, and leave it for three days;
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then he unties it, and makes it move gently, until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The knee is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inward and outward, and backward;
et ne desalue point devant.	and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign of this is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the thigh, and if it does not straighten at the thigh, know that it is dislocated;
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his face, and put his foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee properly;
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another minister extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he holds his leg lightly to his thigh;
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and apply the plaster on it, and bind the leg to the thigh tightly, and keep them tied together for three or four days, then untie it;
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and the patient does not strain to walk until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not fully healed, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is mended.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes displaced, and sometimes fully dislocated, both internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	and the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and you should examine where it has dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The movement is light, and it must be extended lightly by hand when it is merely awakened.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is entirely dislocated, then you must make the patient sit straight, and have the assistant hold the leg by the ankle above the foot;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with the left two times, then stretch it upwards, and gently push the foot upwards;
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this two times, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot;
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	if it returns, that is good;
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if not, then repeat the procedure, for it will return;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return thus, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and fix a peg firmly in the ground between his thighs, and wrap cloths around so that it does not hurt the patient;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then have one minister hold the thigh, and another minister extend the foot with his hands or at the joint that is tied above the ankle;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then have each minister extend equally, and the peg should be between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when they are being stretched;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then let the physician place his hands equally on the dislocation, and another minister hold the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is at the right point, put the plaster and bandages on, bind tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the heel behind, so that the binding is not too tight;
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	then leave it for two days or three, and if the binding softens, then bind tightly again;
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient to walk for four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he walks before that time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses come, you must soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both are dislocated, they must be extended well without effort, and this is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the foot's back, then you must make the patient sit on a flat place or on a table straight, and put your foot on what appears of these joints, then press with your foot firmly until it returns;
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	and when it is leveled and nothing appears, then put under the sole of the foot a board at two shillings, then bind it properly, and leave it for three days, then untie it;
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and make it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	do not be presumptuous in the care, if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and cautious, not bold;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and begin with things that soothe the hot abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands if you see no hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope there, reset now the limb to its place, unless the abscess begins to heat up;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, administer soothing things for a hot abscess, and treat the wound as appropriate with drying ointments;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if with the dislocation there is a fracture and small bones are displaced, remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and beware of entering the way of fear, according to what I have said, for it is worth moving according to your Creator, and for the wisdom of your arm and your body.
